<div id="review_22965638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22965638" />
    <a title="C." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1186674-c"><img alt="C." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302133592p2/1186674.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22965638?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C." class="user" itemprop="url" name="C." href="/user/show/1186674-c">C.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1186674-c?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22965638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17797024144385040330">This is one of my favorite novels, even though it is definitely not one of the best novels I've read.<br/><br/>When I read anything, I tend to enjoy it more when the character development is strong enough that I care about what the characters think and feel, and especially what happens to them.<br/><br/>Anne McCaffrey may be weak at creating actual science fiction—I consider this book to be more of a futuristic fantasy than hard science fiction—but she is fantastic at showing you who a character is as a person, and</span>
  <span id="freeText17797024144385040330" style="display:none">This is one of my favorite novels, even though it is definitely not one of the best novels I've read.<br /><br />When I read anything, I tend to enjoy it more when the character development is strong enough that I care about what the characters think and feel, and especially what happens to them.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey may be weak at creating actual science fiction—I consider this book to be more of a futuristic fantasy than hard science fiction—but she is fantastic at showing you who a character is as a person, and telling stories about people instead of about some clever idea he has, which almost always makes a novel weak.<br /><br />McCaffrey has a fairly optimistic view of what it would be like to have people in the universe that had telepathic, empathic, telekinetic, etc. abilities and how they would benefit all aspects of society. The story follows the main character—an orphan called The Rowan—through her very early years into adulthood, exploring the challenges a uniquely strong Talent would face in her life, and explores what it might mean to have extremely strong telepathic plus telekinetic "Talents" that, with assistance, can literally reach across light years. <br /><br />The primary flaw with this novel is that The Rowan suddenly changes from a mostly sympathetic character in Part One of the novel to (for lack of a better term) a harridan in Part Two. I believe the main reason for this sudden shift is that originally the novel was a short story that starts where Part Two of this novel starts, and McCaffrey needed a more likable character for the extended story, but wanted to retain the spirit of the original. In Part Three she settles into a more moderate character that feels like an averaging of the two personalities that appears earlier in the book.<br /><br />I liked the whole series which is usually called "The Tower and the Hive" series, even though the last novel feels more like a "tying up loose ends" story than anything. However, this book easily stands on its own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17797024144385040330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_538126515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/538126515" />
    <a title="Charlee Allden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17535354-charlee-allden"><img alt="Charlee Allden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429406981p2/17535354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538126515?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlee Allden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlee Allden" href="/user/show/17535354-charlee-allden">Charlee Allden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17535354-charlee-allden?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17535354-charlee-allden?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538126515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12835112052114619716">The Rowan by Anne McCaffrey is the first novel I ever read that I could not put down. I read it straight through cover to cover. I do that fairly often these days, but at the time it was an event that rocked my world. I once heard a male sci-fi author call McCaffrey’s books a gateway drug for getting girls into sci-fi, but for me this book clued me in on what was missing from the sci-fi books I’d already been reading—romance. The Rowan catapulted to the top of my all time favorites list and here</span>
  <span id="freeText12835112052114619716" style="display:none">The Rowan by Anne McCaffrey is the first novel I ever read that I could not put down. I read it straight through cover to cover. I do that fairly often these days, but at the time it was an event that rocked my world. I once heard a male sci-fi author call McCaffrey’s books a gateway drug for getting girls into sci-fi, but for me this book clued me in on what was missing from the sci-fi books I’d already been reading—romance. The Rowan catapulted to the top of my all time favorites list and here’s why….<br /><br />What I love about the heroine:<br /><br />Rowan is a lonely young woman, with incredible psychic gifts, who takes herself too seriously at times. Doesn’t sound like heroine material right? But it makes her very relatable. Trust me on this. She also has courage, always manages to rise above events, and steps up to the plate to save the world and her hero.<br /><br />What I love about the hero:<br /><br />Jeff Raven is a mystery man who calls out to his heroine across space. He matches her for psychic abilities and courage with a touch of charming arrogance added in. Besides, he is struggling desperately to save his people, what could be more heroic?<br /><br />Other cool stuff I like about this story:<br /><br />The psychics in this book are charged with making space travel happen. They push cargo and passenger vessels through space with their minds. Cool!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12835112052114619716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46008876-ijm?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1396398145&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1396398145" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16873995900039446580">This book left me frustrated. On the one hand, you have this great world building by the author. I wanted to know so much more about the universe of the book. The main character was intriguing as well. The first half of the book as really interesting. The second half morphed into a love story that seemed really quick and felt very heavy handed. Events like an alien invasion are sped through to dedicate more time to the love story of Rowan and Jeff. And personally, I just felt like the talents jo</span>
  <span id="freeText16873995900039446580" style="display:none">This book left me frustrated. On the one hand, you have this great world building by the author. I wanted to know so much more about the universe of the book. The main character was intriguing as well. The first half of the book as really interesting. The second half morphed into a love story that seemed really quick and felt very heavy handed. Events like an alien invasion are sped through to dedicate more time to the love story of Rowan and Jeff. And personally, I just felt like the talents joining forces together to destroy massive alien bugs was more interesting than The Rowan and Jeff being all lovey-dovey with each other. <br /><br />I also wasn't sure how we were supposed to dislike Siglen because she was difficult to her staff, but forgive The Rowan for being difficult with her staff. It's also very interesting that Siglen's plus size body and wanting to make sure The Rowan was never hungry is presented as part of her character/moral failings. Also, Jeff was very condescending. We're told we're supposed to find him charming, without him actually saying or doing anything charming. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16873995900039446580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I read this book and loved it and it basically was the spark that started my love of reading. I have rea</span>
  <span id="freeText12596282322973319557" style="display:none">The only reason I picked up this book was because there was a short story in Get off the Unicorn and it peaked my interest - I was NOT a reader. I read this book and loved it and it basically was the spark that started my love of reading. While it reads almost like a biography, going from infancy through to marriage and all the struggles in between of a talented girl and the expectations thrust up on her, the world Anne McCaffrey has created and her characters leaves you wanting more. I have read this book many times, have had to replace my mass market copy and expect I will read it many more times. A must read for any reader, regardless of your preferred genre. </span>

  <span id="freeText9478753814984156445" style="display:none">This is one of my all-time favorite books. I first read it when I was 13 or 14 and continued to pick up Anne McCafrey's entire catalog afterwards. I've read it every few years since (I'm now 34) and still adore it! I even have a signed copy from when I met Ms. McCaffrey back ing 2005. Sadly, the reason I picked it up again was because Ms. McCaffrey passed away just a few days ago - on November 21, 2011. It seemed fitting to read it again now as a celebration of her life and the role she played in turning a young girl into an avid reader.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13360688917421157545">The first Anne McCaffrey book I've actually finished (I started Pern twice when I was younger but always got distracted by other books). <br/>Overall the coming-of-age setup for this book was more interesting than the actual series plot which as of the end of book 1 is just "generic aliens attack because they're evil or something; manic pixie dream boy arrives on the scene; main character gets pregnant and decides to have as many kids as possible <s>for no reason</s> because the rest of the series is going </span>
  <span id="freeText13360688917421157545" style="display:none">The first Anne McCaffrey book I've actually finished (I started Pern twice when I was younger but always got distracted by other books). <br>Overall the coming-of-age setup for this book was more interesting than the actual series plot which as of the end of book 1 is just "generic aliens attack because they're evil or something; manic pixie dream boy arrives on the scene; main character gets pregnant and decides to have as many kids as possible <s>for no reason</s> because the rest of the series is going to be about her descendants". <br>I won't go out of my way to read the rest of the series, but if I happen to stumble across book 2 somewhere I'll probably read it.<br><br>Also fun fact the edition I read had orange text and isn't on goodreads... pretty sure it's this one: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1565151111i/27949585._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('juI85HSWS0HIBWSL1eAB9dgYhOk061RsoYWbVi9sPaKO37bj2u20X6DlRx+o/HBeS0RlF9ZnxsaW2ELNCfP0OQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZHKA7l4B+aU2dAesy/aInE8dhzbETu2Ozvo95iwkX4ZkTwrp8HoGu16UJDi26vk33EFmyCbCfyT5p+R9CruWHQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">About Anne McCaffrey</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1599324585p3/26.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">Anne McCaffrey
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9230600116774679277">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br/><br/>Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText9230600116774679277" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br /><br />Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High School in Montclair, New Jersey, and graduated cum laude from Radcliffe College, majoring in Slavonic Languages and Literatures.<br /><br />Her working career included Liberty Music Shops and Helena Rubinstein (1947-1952). She married in 1950 and had three children: Alec Anthony, b. 1952, Todd, b.1956, and Georgeanne, b.1959.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey’s first story was published by Sam Moskowitz in Science Fiction + Magazine and her first novel was published by Ballantine Books in 1967. By the time the three children of her marriage were comfortably in school most of the day, she had already achieved enough success with short stories to devote full time to writing. Her first novel, Restoree, was written as a protest against the absurd and unrealistic portrayals of women in s-f novels in the 50s and early 60s. It is, however, in the handling of broader themes and the worlds of her imagination, particularly the two series The Ship Who Sang and the fourteen novels about the Dragonriders of Pern that Ms. McCaffrey’s talents as a story-teller are best displayed.<br /><br />She died at the age of 85, after suffering a massive stroke on 21 November 2011.<br /><br />Obituaries: <a href="http://www.locusmag.com/News/2011/11/anne-mccaffrey-1926-2011/" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a>, <a href="http://www.mediabistro.com/galleycat/anne-mccaffrey-has-died_b42826" rel="nofollow noopener">GalleyCat</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9230600116774679277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
